## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science / solid mechanics (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: With sigma as stress, epsilon as strain, and T as temperature, the task matches constitutive stress–strain laws with thermal effects (temperature-dependent stiffness/yield and thermal expansion/softening). Likely relationships include elastic/visco-plastic hardening in epsilon modulated by T and thermal strain offsets proportional to (T - T0).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear elastic (Hooke): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elasticity at fixed T)
- Elastic with temperature-dependent modulus (linear-in-T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (stiffness changes with temperature)
- Elastic with temperature-dependent modulus (reciprocal form): sigma = (c0 / (T + c1)) * epsilon (stiffness decreases with increasing T, avoiding constants in denominators)
- Thermoelastic with thermal strain offset: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (thermal expansion reduces mechanical strain)
- Polynomial nonlinear elasticity: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (moderate-strain nonlinearity)
- Hyperelastic (neo-Hookean-like using stretch 1+epsilon): sigma = c0 * ((1 + epsilon) - (1 + epsilon)**(-2)) (rubber-like response, large strain)
- Hollomon power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (plastic/work hardening; c1 prevents singularity near 0 strain)
- Ramberg–Osgood implicit form (inverted for sigma): sigma = c0 * (epsilon / (c1 + epsilon))**c2 (smooth transition from elastic to plastic-like hardening)
- Thermal softening multiplicative factor: sigma = (c0 * epsilon**c1) * (c2 - c3 * T) (hardening in strain with linear softening in temperature)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = (c0 * epsilon**c1) * exp(c2 * T) (monotone T effect; c2 typically negative for softening)
- Johnson–Cook-like strain hardening with thermal softening (no strain-rate term): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * (1 - c5 * T)**c6) (combined hardening and melting/softening-style factor)
- WLF-style temperature shift on effective strain (polymer-like): sigma = c0 * (epsilon * exp(c1 * (T - c2) / (T - c2 + c3)))**c4 (time-temperature equivalence encoded as a T-dependent strain scaling)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal expansion appears as an additive strain shift: sigma depends on (epsilon - c * (T - T0)); at higher T the same applied epsilon yields lower sigma.
- Temperature-dependent stiffness is commonly multiplicative: sigma = E(T) * epsilon, where E(T) often decreases roughly linearly or hyperbolically with T over a limited range.
- Plastic/work hardening often follows concave power laws in epsilon: sigma ~ (epsilon + c)^n with 0 < n < 1 (diminishing hardening rate).
- Smooth elastic-to-plastic transition can be modeled by rational-in-epsilon maps like (epsilon/(epsilon+c))^n to avoid kinks while capturing yield-like curvature.
- Large-strain polymer/elastomer behavior is better captured by functions of stretch (1+epsilon) and inverse powers, producing strong upturn at high tension and reduced stress in compression.
- Thermal softening frequently enters as a bounded factor that tends toward zero near a characteristic temperature (e.g., melt/transition), motivating terms like (1 - c*T)^m clipped to physical range.
- If sigma decreases with T at fixed epsilon, structures with exp(c*T) (c<0) or (c0 - c1*T) are typical; if sigma increases (e.g., entropic elasticity), the sign flips.
- Coupled effects often require multiplicative separation: sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T) rather than additive f(epsilon)+g(T), reflecting that temperature scales the whole stress level.
